Phrases

This section collects all the sacred phrases I've learned over the years.

I use the word "phrase" to describe what is often known as a mantra - a short, complete saying used in devotional practice. For example, oá¹ tÄre tuttÄre ture svÄhÄ is a single phrase directed to ÄryatÄrÄ.

Rather than using the word "prayer", which can sometimes suggest a full ritual sequence or structured worship service, I focus here on the spoken invocations themselves - the concise expressions of devotion, intention, and reverence.

Each phrase listed is a distinct spiritual utterance, often associated with a particular deity, purpose, or blessing. Whether used on its own or as part of a larger practice, each one stands as a meaningful and complete act of connection.

Bhaiá¹£ajyaguru is the Buddha of healing and medicine in MahÄyÄna Buddhism, who cures suffering (duá¸¥kha) using the medicine of his teachings.

BodhigarbhaÌlamÌ£kaÌralaksÌ£aâ

bodhi bodhi à¥¤ bodhanÄ« bodhanÄ« à¥¤ sarva tathÄgata gocarÄ« à¥¤ dhara dhara à¥¤ hara hara à¥¤ prahara prahara à¥¤ mahÄ bodhicitta dhÄre à¥¤ culu culu à¥¤ Åata raÅmi saÃ±codite à¥¤ sarva tathÄgatÄbhiá¹£ikte à¥¤ guá¹Ä« guá¹apate à¥¤ sarva buddha guá¹ÄvabhÄse à¥¤ mili mili à¥¤ gaganatale à¥¤ sarva tathÄgatÄdhiá¹£á¹­hite à¥¤ nabhasthale à¥¤ Åame Åame à¥¤ praÅame praÅame à¥¤ sarva pÄpam praÅame à¥¤ sarva pÄpaá¹ viÅodhane à¥¤ hulu hulu à¥¤ mahÄbodhi mÄrga sampratiá¹£á¹­hite à¥¤ sarva tathÄgata supratiá¹£á¹­hite Åuddhe svÄhÄ à¥¤ oá¹ sarva tathÄgata vyavalokite à¥¤ jaya jaya svÄhÄ à¥¤ oá¹ dhuru dhuru jayamukhe svÄhÄ à¥¤ oá¹ vajrÄyuá¹£e svÄhÄà¥¥

By putting even just one prayer of the BodhigarbhaÌlamÌ£kaÌralaksÌ£a inside a stupa, it brings the same merit as having built 100,000 stupas - whether the stupa is gigantic like Bodh GayÄ or tiny like the size of a finger. Then, if you dedicate this merit for sentient beings, for their happiness up to full enlightenment, they receive unbelievable benefits and you receive unbelievable merit.

One collects the merit of having made offerings to all the Buddhas, to all the Dharma, and to all the Sangha. Because when you make offerings to a stupa containing the 100,000 Ornaments of Enlightenment prayer, you are not only making offering to a stupa. It becomes an offering to the Three Rare Sublime Ones - all the Buddha, Dharma, and Sangha that exist in the ten directions, in any universe.

Having made offerings to as many Buddhas as there are in ninety-nine sesame seed pods - that is how much merit we create and we are always guided by that many Buddhas.

MahÄ CundÄ« DurgÄ DhÄranÄ«â

oá¹ cale cule cunde svÄhÄà¥¥

CundÄ« is a female Indian Buddhist deity which remains popular in East Asian Buddhism. In Chinese Buddhism, she is associated with the practice of the well known CundÄ« dhÄraá¹Ä«, which is performed along with a specific mudra (hand gesture), as well as the use of a circular mirror. She is considered to be able to purify negative karma, provide protection, support spiritual practice which allows one to quickly attain Buddhahood.

The Emerald Buddha (Chinese: çä½, Thai: à¸à¸£à¸°à¹à¸à¹à¸§à¸¡à¸£à¸à¸) is a statuette that portrays the historical Buddha ÅÄkyamuni, clothed in gold and seated on the throne under a five-tiered chatra, and is sculpted from an unknown green stone (most likely jasper rather than emerald), its perceived powers are of epic proportions. One of the jewels of the Chakravartin, it is also arguably the most sacred Buddhist icon in mainland Southeast Asia.

MahÄmaá¹i VipulavimÄnaâ

oá¹ vipulagarbhe maá¹iprabhe tathÄgatanidarÅane à¥¤ maá¹i maá¹i suprabhe vimale sÄgara gambhÄ«re hÅ«á¹ hÅ«á¹ jvÄla jvÄla à¥¤ buddhÄvilokite guhyÄdhiá¹£á¹­ita garbhe svÄhÄ à¥¤ padmadhara amogha jayate curu curu svÄhÄ à¥¤ oá¹ maá¹ivajre hÅ«á¹ à¥¤ oá¹ maá¹idhare hÅ«á¹ phaá¹­ à¥¤ oá¹ maá¹ipadme hÅ«á¹ hrÄ«á¸¥ arapacamita há¹daya svÄhÄ à¥¤ oá¹ hanu pÄÅa bhÄra há¹daya svÄhÄà¥¥

The Buddha achieves nirvana and subdued demons with this prayer. Any being who sees, recites, hears, touches, or wears this victorious prayer will purify their negative karmas or unholy obstacles.

MahÄvairocana Sarvadurgati PariÅodhana DhÄraá¹Ä«â

oá¹ Åodhani Åodhani à¥¤ sarva pÄpaá¹ viÅodhani à¥¤ Åuddhe viÅuddhe à¥¤ sarva karma Ävaraá¹a viÅodhani svÄhÄà¥¥

Vairocana is seen as the dharmakÄya (the supreme buddha-body, the body of ultimate reality), and the embodiment of the Buddhist concept of wisdom and purity. In the conception of the Five Jinas of Mahayana and Vajrayana Buddhism, Vairocana is at the centre and is often considered a Primordial Buddha. In East Asian esoteric Buddhism, MahÄvairocana is considered to be a cosmic Buddha whose body is the entire universe, the DharmadhÄtu.

MaÃ±juÅrÄ« Há¹dayaâ

oá¹ arapacana dhÄ«á¸¥à¥¥

This prayer will open 5 Dharma doors:

  • Ädya-anutpannatvÄd (a door to the insight that all dharmas are unproduced from the very beginning)
  • rajas (a door to the insight that all dharmas are without dirt)
  • paramÄrtha (a door to the insight that all dharmas have been expounded in the ultimate sense)
  • cyavana (a door to the insight that the decrease or rebirth of any dharma cannot be apprehended, because all dharmas do not decrease, nor are they reborn)
  • nÄma (a door to the insight that the names of all dharmas have vanished; the essential nature behind names cannot be gained or lost)

This prayer is believed to enhance wisdom and improve one's skills in debating, memory, writing, and other literary abilities.

Oá¹ Five Dharma Doors, DhÄ«á¸¥!

PaÃ±ca Jambhalaâ

oá¹ jambhala jalendraye svÄhÄà¥¥Â oá¹ jambhala jalendraye dhanam medhÄ« hrÄ«á¸¥ á¸ÄkinÄ« jambhala sambhara svÄhÄà¥¥Â oá¹ jambhala jalendraye vasudhÄriá¹Ä« svÄhÄà¥¥Â oá¹ padma krodha Ärya jambhala há¹daya hÅ«á¹ phaá¹­à¥¥Â oá¹ karma jambhala Äá¸¥ svÄhÄà¥¥

The five Jambhalas are the manifestations of the compassion of Buddhas and Bodhisattvas to guide sentient beings along the path to enlightenment. They have the essence of generosity and represent the activities of increasing benefit. Their aspirations are to help the poor and those suffering from ill-fortune.

à¼à¼à¼ à¼à½¨à½¼à½¾à¼à½à½à¾¨à½¼à¼à½¨à½´à½¥à¾à½±à½²à¼à½¥à¼à½à½²à¼à½à¼à½£à½²à¼à½§à½±à½´à¾à¼à½à½à¼

PaÃ±caÅÄ«laâ

pÄá¹ÄtipÄtÄ veramaá¹Ä« sikkhÄpadaá¹ samÄdiyÄmi à¥¤ adinnÄdÄnÄ veramaá¹Ä« sikkhÄpadaá¹ samÄdiyÄmi à¥¤ kÄmesumicchÄcÄra veramaá¹Ä« sikkhÄpadaá¹ samÄdiyÄmi à¥¤ musÄvÄdÄ veramaá¹Ä« sikkhÄpadaá¹ samÄdiyÄmi à¥¤ surÄmeraya majjapamÄdaá¹­á¹­hÄnÄ veramaá¹Ä« sikkhÄpadaá¹ samÄdiyÄmià¥¥

The easiest way to avoid new karma debts is to follow five precepts. Think of them like gentle reminders to stay kind and careful:

  1. Don't hurt living beings Every creature wants to live. Be gentle with people, animals, even tiny bugs.
  2. Don't take what isn't yours If it doesn't belong to you, leave it. Sharing is good, stealing is not.
  3. Don't break trust in love Be honest and kind in friendships and relationships. Don't cause harm with your choices.
  4. Don't lie Words can heal or hurt. Speak the truth, and use words to help, not harm.
  5. Don't cloud your mind Stay clear and mindful. Avoid things that make you lose control or forget kindness.

Following these five precepts is like keeping your balance sheet clean. No new debts, no new troubles - just more peace and freedom.

PratÄ«tyasamutpÄda GÄthÄâ

ye dharmÄ hetuprabhavÄ hetuá¹ teá¹£Äá¹ tathÄgata uvÄca à¥¤ teá¹£Äá¹-ca yo nirodha evaá¹vÄdi mahÄÅramaá¹aá¸¥ à¥¤ ajÃ±ÄnÄc cÄ«yate karma janmanaá¸¥ karma kÄraá¹am à¥¤ jÃ±ÄnÄn na cÄ«yate karma karmÄbhÄvÄn na jÄyateà¥¥
7x

Dependent origination can be contrasted with the classic Western concept of causation in which an action by one thing is said to cause a change in another thing. Dependent origination instead views the change as being caused by many factors, not just one or even a few.

Those dharmas which arise from a cause, the TathÄgata has declared their cause.
And that which is the cessation of them, thus the great renunciant (sramana) has taught.
Through ignorance, karma is accumulated, karma is the cause of (re)birth.
Through knowledge, karma is not accumulated, through absence of karma, one is not (re)born.

The additional verse is Southeast Asia specific (fifth century date) and does not have an equivalent in any Buddhist text, whether in the original Indic language or Tibetan or Chinese translation.

RaÅmi Vimala ViÅuddha PrabhÄ NÄma DhÄraá¹Ä«â

namo sapta saptatibhyaá¸¥ à¥¤ samyaksaá¹buddha koá¹­inÄá¹ pariÅuddha manasa à¥¤ vÄcitta pratiá¹£á¹­itÄnÄá¹ à¥¤ namo bhagavate amitÄyuá¹£asya tathÄgatasya à¥¤ oá¹ tathÄgata Åuddhe ÄyuviÅuddhani à¥¤ saá¹hÄra saá¹hÄra à¥¤ sarva tathÄgata vÄ«rya valeda prati saá¹hÄra à¥¤ Äyu smara smara à¥¤ sarva tathÄgata samayaá¹ à¥¤ bodhi bodhi à¥¤ buddhyÄ vibuddhyÄ à¥¤ bodhaya bodhaya à¥¤ sarva satvanÄá¹ à¥¤ sarva pÄpÄ varaá¹a viÅuddhe à¥¤ vigatamÄra bhayaá¹ à¥¤ subuddhÄ buddhe huru huru svÄhÄà¥¥

RaÅmi Vimala ViÅuddha PrabhÄ NÄma DhÄraá¹Ä« purifies the five uninterrupted negative karmas.

If this prayer is put inside a stupa then any being, including evil transmigratory beings, who sees the stupa, hears of the stupa, touches the stupa, or who is touched by dust or wind that comes from this stupa, will be free from all negative karmas. They will be born in the realms of happy transmigratory beings and they won't be reborn in the lower realms.

If one offers even a bell to a stupa containing this prayer, all the sentient beings in that area, animals or humans, by hearing the sound of that bell will be completely purified of the five uninterrupted negative karmas. Even just thinking about the stupa purifies the five uninterrupted negative karmas.

RaÅmi Vimala ViÅuddha PrabhÄ NÄma Há¹daya purifies the five uninterrupted negative karmas.

The Six DharmakÄya Relics1 is a collection of five classes of great dhÄraá¹Ä«s2 and Kriyayogatantra - Immaculate Radiance3, as the most important relic of the dharmakÄya4, must be inserted together in every Buddha statue/stupa/sculpture. The five classes of great dhÄraá¹Ä«s2 are:

  1. Uá¹£á¹Ä«á¹£avijayÄ5
  2. Vimala Uá¹£á¹Ä«á¹£a6
  3. GuhyadhaÌtukaranÌ£dÌ£a7
  4. BodhigarbhÄlaá¹kÄralaká¹£a8
  5. PratÄ«tyasamutpÄdahá¹daya9

A Buddha statue/stupa/sculpture which has been consecrated and energised by the relics of dharmakÄya4 is no longer a man-made monument but a sacred entity that can bestow blessings and amplify the potentiality of benefits, restore positive conditions for anyone who sponsor its construction, see it, touch it, circumambulate it, or hear the breeze that blow by it.

oá¹ amá¹te à¥¤ amá¹ta udbhave à¥¤ amá¹ta saá¹bhave à¥¤ amá¹ta garbhe à¥¤ amá¹ta siddhe à¥¤ amá¹ta teje à¥¤ amá¹ta vikrÄnte à¥¤ amá¹ta vikrÄnta gÄmine à¥¤ amá¹ta gagana ká¹tikare à¥¤ amá¹ta duá¹dubhi svare à¥¤ sarva artha sÄdhane à¥¤ sarva karma kleÅa ká¹£ayaá¹kare svÄhÄ à¥¤ oá¹ amitÄbha hrÄ«á¸¥à¥¥

Buddha of longevity, purification, and rebirths in Buddhism. She wears an image of Vairocana in her headdress. With Amitayus and White Tara, she constitutes one of the three Buddhas of Long Life.

VajragÄ«tÄâ

ema kiri kiri à¥¤ mashta vÄli vÄli à¥¤ samita suru suru à¥¤ kutali masu masu à¥¤ ekara suli bhatayÃ© à¥¤ cakira bhuli bhatayÃ© à¥¤ samunta carya sughayÃ© à¥¤ bhetasana bhyakulayÃ© à¥¤ sakari dhukana à¥¤ matari vaitana à¥¤ parali hisana à¥¤ makharta kelanam à¥¤ sambhara tameka cantapa à¥¤ surya bhatare pashanapa à¥¤ ranabhiti saghuralapa à¥¤ masmin sagulitayapa à¥¤ ghura ghura saga kharnalam à¥¤ nara nara ithar patalam à¥¤ sirna sirna bhesa raspalam à¥¤ bhundha bhundha cisha sakelam à¥¤ sasah à¥¤ ririh à¥¤ lilih à¥¤ i ih à¥¤ mimih à¥¤ ra ra rahà¥¥

This dharmatÄ song evokes the wisdom of Ädibuddha in union to channel our energies towards the goal of spiritual enlightenment.

The union is generally understood to represent the primordial (or mystical) union of compassion and wisdom, depicted as a male deity in union with his female consort through the similar ideas of interpenetration or coalescence (Sanskrit: à¤¯à¥à¤à¤¨à¤¦à¥à¤§, Romanized: Yuganaddha, Chinese: éé£, Tibetan: à½à½´à½à¼à½ à½à½´à½, Wylie: zung-'jug, THL: zunjuk), using the concept of Indra's net to illustrate this.

The symbolism is associated with Anuttarayoga tantra and while there are various interpretations of the symbolism in twilight language, the masculine figure is representing the compassion (karuá¹Ä) and skillful means (upÄya-kauÅalya) that have to be developed in order to reach enlightenment. While the feminine partner is representing wisdom (prajÃ±Ä) which is also necessary to enlightenment. United, the figures symbolize the union necessary to overcome the veils of Maya, the false duality of object and subject.

Without birth and so without cease,
Not coming or going, but filling all,
Blissful dharma sublime and unmoving,
Sky-like, freed and without stain,
Rootless, and also without support,
Homeless, unattached, a dharma profound,
Ever free, ever vast, equality effortless,
Subject to neither bondage nor liberation,
An ever present palace encompassing all,
Beyond logic and reason.
So vast, so grand, the space of the sky!
Blazing dharma, the core of the sun and the moon,
Instant presence, now it's so plain to see,
A mountain of vajra, a lotus so immense,
The sun, a lion, this wisdom song.
A sound so great, a music beyond compare,
A pleasure reaching to the ends of space,
A Buddha equal to all of the Buddhas,
Samantabhadra the vast, the peak of dharma,
In the womb of SamantabhadrÄ«, her sky-like space,
Open clarity, instantly presentâthe ever great perfection!
